  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_567a9841-1fd7-4c05-812a-2b6c3832e404'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<div class='spoiler'>
This question contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a href="/questions/866266-is-it-ever-explained-why-bran-hated-eamonn"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Is it ever explained why Bran hated Eamonn so much? He seemed to have something against Eamonn simply because Eamonn's father was a traitor. It seemed to me that if anyone was justified to hold a grudge in this book it was Eamonn. Bran killed his men, got the girl he was in love with, and hates his guts simply because he carries his father's genes...I am genuinely confused by this. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></a>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/7424601-ann-marie"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1326528619i/7424601._UX100_CR0,2,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/7424601-ann-marie">Ann-Marie</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Hi! Bran was being paid to torment Eamonn, but he was also a good judge of character. He had recruited a young man called Rat into his team - Rat's ba<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Hi! Bran was being paid to torment Eamonn, but he was also a good judge of character. He had recruited a young man called Rat into his team - Rat's backstory goes that Eamonn killed his mother, father and little sisters, when he was trying to payback an enemy. Bran knew of this. It was mentioned that Eamonn had double crossed other people too. <br /><br />Also, Eamonn's character was to carry out the theme of son's following in their father's footsteps. This was an example of how Eamonn's father was bad - manipulative, devious, underhanded- and Eamonn was also that way inclined. Likewise John who was Bran's father was good - thus Bran was able to take up his rightful heritage at the end of the story. Finally, he is a pretty interesting and complex villain!! I couldn't believe he'd still offer marriage to Liadan after her son was born!!! <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_1144256050" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1144256050" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1144256050?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fae">fae</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1144256050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2512168810574367556"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Don't you long for something different to happen, something so exciting and new it carries you along with it like a great tide, something that lets your life blaze and burn so the whole world can see it?”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/>Where do I start?How can I put into words <b>the magnitude of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8649.Juliet_Marillier' title='Juliet Marillier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Juliet Marillier</a>'s writing</b>?How can I explain to someone who hasn't lived through her books that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13927.Son_of_the_Shadows__Sevenwaters___2_' title='Son of the Shadows (Sevenwaters, #2) by Juliet Marillier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Son of the Shadows</a> left me a <b>sobbing mess</b>,that there were scenes so <b>emotionally brutal</b> and <b>devastating</b> that it felt like my hear</span>
  <span id="freeText2512168810574367556" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Don't you long for something different to happen, something so exciting and new it carries you along with it like a great tide, something that lets your life blaze and burn so the whole world can see it?”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>Where do I start?How can I put into words <b>the magnitude of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8649.Juliet_Marillier" title="Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Juliet Marillier</a>'s writing</b>?How can I explain to someone who hasn't lived through her books that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13927.Son_of_the_Shadows__Sevenwaters___2_" title="Son of the Shadows (Sevenwaters, #2) by Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Son of the Shadows</a> left me a <b>sobbing mess</b>,that there were scenes so <b>emotionally brutal</b> and <b>devastating</b> that it felt like my heart was ripped from my chest and squeezed until there was no blood left?And that despite the <b>pain</b> and the <b>agony</b>,I felt <b>pure</b> in the end?<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Come, dear heart.Lean on me and let us walk this path together.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>Together.The Sevenwaters family,Red and Sorcha's family believed that there would be no evil in the world they could not face together.And that is precisely the reason the evil forces tried to divide them,to wreak havoc and mistrust on a family that valued their bond more than anything else.Secrets and betrayals came to light,one by one,threading a web of isolation and anger.Liadan,Sorcha's dutiful daughter,the healer with the Sight,was caught in the middle of it.For it was her the Fair Folk had been waiting for generations to help fulfill an ancient prophecy.But Liadan was no mere tool.Nor was Bran,despite everyone's efforts to convince her otherwise.<b>Warriors,druids,mercenaries,misguided girls,they were all woven in a pattern and Liadan held the key to either destruction or salvation.</b><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Your actions are your own.Your choices are your own.Each of us carries a burden of guilt for decisions made or not made.You can let that rule your whole life or you can put it behind you and move on.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><b>This was not a happy story</b>.Sorcha's courage and sacrifice held her family together,but they were not enough.Liadan on the other hand wasn't as willing as her mother to follow the path the Fair Folk chose for her.She was a strong and independent woman,she made her choices against everyone's warnings.But she loved fiercely,like her parents did.And while Bran wasn't Prince Charming,just a scary and equally scared man consumed by hatred and bloodlust,he was perfect for her,and she for him.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“He and I…we share a bond. Not love, exactly. It goes beyond that. He is mine as surely as sun follows moon across the sky. Mine before ever I knew he existed. Mine until death and beyond.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I try to swallow my grief for everything that happened,but my feelings are overwhelming and difficult to control.My heart breaks for the trials my heroes had to face,but I keep admiring them for their strength.Conor made some huge mistakes,and so did Red,and Liam,and Sean,and Niahm but I cannot blame them,not when they thought they did the right thing for the people they loved.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The world is simple in its essence. Life,death,love,hate.Desire,fulfillment.Magic.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>All of these elements combined make this story a unique one,like the tales your grandfather used to tell you by the hearth.<b>Irish mythology entangled with high fantasy,the ancient battle between Good and Evil and the mortals in between</b> made an extraordinary book,one of those that stay with you forever.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446470046ra/16813534.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="2512168810574367556" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1230793317" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1230793317" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1230793317?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11796524-son-of-the-shadows">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Team Darkling</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=buddy-reads-are-the-best">buddy-reads-are-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=that-bastard">that-bastard</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=rabid-reads-reviews">rabid-reads-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1230793317" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5612220116332533069"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2015/04/review-son-of-the-shadows-by-juliet-marillier.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/><b>BR with my peeps at: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Buddies Books and Baubles</a></b><br/><br/><b>Specifically:</b> <b>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
</b><br/><br/><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Sometimes when I finish a book I know <i>exactly</i> what I think about it, and the review practically writes itself. Other times . . . I finish, thinking that <em>overall</em> I liked the book, but . . . something remains . . . unresolved. And the more I dwell on it, the more issues emerge, until the <em>something</em> evolves into multiple identifiable problems.<br/><br/>This is one of <em>those</em> times.<br/><br/>That's not to sa</span>
  <span id="freeText5612220116332533069" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2015/04/review-son-of-the-shadows-by-juliet-marillier.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br><b>BR with my peeps at: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies Books and Baubles</a></b><br><br><b>Specifically:</b> <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
</b><br><br><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br>Sometimes when I finish a book I know <i>exactly</i> what I think about it, and the review practically writes itself. Other times . . . I finish, thinking that <em>overall</em> I liked the book, but . . . something remains . . . unresolved. And the more I dwell on it, the more issues emerge, until the <em>something</em> evolves into multiple identifiable problems.<br><br>This is one of <em>those</em> times.<br><br>That's not to say that <em>Son of the Shadows</em> wasn't a good book. It absolutely was.<br><br>It just wasn't a good book <i>for me</i>.<br><br>There are several reasons.<br><br>I didn't particularly like either this generation from Sevenwaters <em>or</em> several of the other important new characters.<br><br>Sorcha and Red, the MCs from the previous installment, now have three grown children: their eighteen-year-old firstborn Niamh, and sixteen-year-old twins Sean and Liadan. Sean is the heir of Sevenwaters, Liadan has followed in her mother's footsteps as a healer and is the "heart" of Sevenwaters, and Niamh is the petulant beauty with a nasty mean streak.<br><br>Does Niamh have understandable reasons for lashing out at others and placing most of her self-worth in her appearance?<br><br>Yes. She does. <br><br>In fact, she'd make a perfect villain. <br><br>I think the best kind of villain is the kind that you can empathize with, but still not <i>like</i>. <br><br>Villains you genuinely like aren't villains. They're anti-heroes. And villainous villains are fun to hate, but there is seldom much depth. Depth allows for empathy, which brings us back full circle.<br><br>But Niamh isn't the villain. <br><br>Instead you're left with a character you don't like, and thus have a hard time drumming up sympathy for when she becomes a victim. <br><br>I recognized cerebrally that what happened to her was awful. But I didn't <i>feel</i> it. Maybe if I had been able to, I would've been distracted from the <i>why</i>, which is what occupied my attention in place of the anguish I might have felt on behalf of a more likable character. <br><br>And the <i>why</i> . . . was pretty flimsy.<br><br>Niamh fell in love with an unsuitable young man. When it was discovered, the relationship was forbidden, but believing that her lover would never forsake her, she was completely shattered when he left.<br><br>"But <i>why</i> did he leave?" you ask, and that's an excellent question. <br><br>It's also a question the adults refuse to answer.<br><br>So later, when Niamh finds herself in abhorrent circumstances, she has nothing to fall back on. She sees herself as worthless, as unworthy of being loved---why else would Unsuitable Lover have abandoned her? Why else would her family have sent her away, turning their backs on her?<br><br>It's . . . infuriating. And ridiculous.<br><br>B/c <i>you</i>, the reader, <i>know</i> why the relationship is forbidden. I actually wondered if my wiring was faulty until my friend Robin (who BR-ed this me) said that she didn't understand what the Big Deal was either. YES, what happened was unfortunate . . . <i>worse</i> than unfortunate. *whispers* Gross, man. But it was a mistake born out of innocence. And, I'm sorry, but that makes a massive difference to me. Robin, too, so there. <br><br>Maybe there are some kind of medieval social connotations we're not aware of, or maybe we're desensitized b/c current events. I don't know. Doesn't matter, really. What <i>does</i> matter is that I didn't buy it.<br><br>Sean was MEH. I appreciated that he thought outside of the box, but he was too irrationally impulsive to <i>like</i>.<br><br>Liadan . . . my feelings in regards to Liadan are complex. <br><br>I should have liked her. I should have <i>loved</i> her. She's exactly the kind of independent-thinking heroine that I usually admire and root unreservedly for.<br><br>And yet . . . I found her condescending. <br><br>My impression wasn’t that she questioned b/c she refused to agree to life-altering decisions without understanding the implications, but that she questioned b/c she-—in her infinite sixteen-year-old wisdom—-knew <i>better</i>. That she was correct didn't matter to me, b/c I'm a brat, and if you do the right thing for the wrong reason . . . (and YES, I'm well aware of the irony).<br><br>And as with Niamh's ignorance making a difference in my perception of her actions, Liadan's motivations made what would have been admirable . . . less so.<br><br>Then there's Bran.<br><br>Bran . . . is an ASS. And not the kind of ASS you find yourself liking against your better judgement, b/c <em>not really</em> an ASS. No, he's the kind of ASS you futilely wanted to like you when you were in high school, despite that fact that he was an ASS, but looking back as an adult, you realize . . . what an <i>ASS</i>.<br><br>And just like High School ASS, Bran has reasons for being an ASS too. Another perfect villain in the making, but, once again, <i>not</i> the villain. <br><br>Which brings me to who <i>was</i> the villain . . . also an ASS, but unlike Bran, if he has reasons, they remain undisclosed. <br><br>My biggest issue also has to do with Villain, but be warned, it's a spoiler:<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Liadan decides to head for Britain with Bran, leaving Villain not just free and loose, but her family ignorant of his treachery, practically insuring their betrayal at his hands at some point in the future, and SHE WON'T EVEN BE THERE b/c BRITAIN. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br> <br>However . . . lots of readers very much enjoy the kind of wounded-bear-type character Bran is, and forgive them everything b/c broken. That is not me. And my dislike of Liadan was based on an vague impression that I can't support with evidence. When I was gearing up for the Buddy Read, several people told me that they loved this book even more than <i>Daughter of the Forest</i>. SO. Take what I've said with a grain of salt. You know your preferences. And you know how critical I can be. Even with my issues, <i>Son of the Shadows</i> wasn't anything I'd consider a <i>bad</i> read, and it wasn't until I started picking things apart that I lowered the rating from 4 stars. Also, I fully intend to read the next book. <br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="5612220116332533069" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1600030158" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1600030158" />
    <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries"><img alt="Mayim de Vries" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560508357p2/50424456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1600030158?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mayim de Vries" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries">Mayim de Vries</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1600030158" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer458450489330515506"><b>The second instalment in the Sevensweaters* series is like an ugly jumper presented by your most favorite aunt. You will never wear it and you will never tell her about it for the sake of good times you spent together.</b><br/><br/>There are six <s>shirts</s> sweaters in the Sevensweaters series. The first one was an enchanted one and the moment you put it on, it put you under a spell. Needless to say, starting the Son of the Shadows I expected a tale of similar quality. What I got instead was a garment badly knitte</span>
  <span id="freeText458450489330515506" style="display:none"><b>The second instalment in the Sevensweaters* series is like an ugly jumper presented by your most favorite aunt. You will never wear it and you will never tell her about it for the sake of good times you spent together.</b><br /><br />There are six <s>shirts</s> sweaters in the Sevensweaters series. The first one was an enchanted one and the moment you put it on, it put you under a spell. Needless to say, starting the Son of the Shadows I expected a tale of similar quality. What I got instead was a garment badly knitted, made of an itchy material, hideous in terms of fabric, colour and patterns. <br /><br /><b>Are you ready for an ugly sweater party? <br /><br />In the middle, the jumper has a huge snowflake</b>. The main heroine, a girl called Liadan (Sorcha's daughter), suffers from the severe "unique one" syndrome, experiencing <i>"nameless feelings of ill; sudden bouts of shivering; cryptic warnings of the mind"</i>. This gift sets her apart from everyone else, and so even though outwardly she expresses the desire to be ordinary, inwardly she relishes in how special she is. Better, wiser, more emphatic/insightful/choose an adjective here/all of the above than everybody else. <br /><br />Apparently, she is also outside the pattern which renders her with an ability to alter the course of things. You see, the rest of us are like puppets implementing grand plans devised by higher beings without an ability to add even a jot to the design. Not Liadan, no. Her actions can challenge and change the destinies. No wonder that a <b>girl raised with this notion reaches mastery at shallow coyness and false modesty that reeks with hypocrisy</b>. <br /><br />This makes her insufferable, but I would endure it of not for one more thing: <b>Liadan's relationship with her sister. The dynamics between the siblings is in a stark contrast with the previous book in the series.</b> Where Sorcha sacrificed everything and suffered for her brothers with love and hope, <b>Liadan's attitude to Niamh is beyond abominable</b>. Mind you, I have a wonderful sister, and so the sisterhood theme is something I can relate to. <br /><br />Liadan at first only complains about Niamh's flaws and incessantly compares herself with the older girl in a way that transforms all Niamh's qualities into vices, then her feelings of being superior culminate in betrayal (even though she never explicitly admits to being the main reason for the terrible events that unfold in the book), followed by an agreement to the unfair treatment Niamh was forced to suffer confessing that she <i>"had scarce given her [sister] a moment's thought"</i> since bidding her farewell. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[What I hated the most, is the fact that while Liadan's transgressions and mistakes were far more severe and consequential than Niamh's actions, the other sister never received the love and warmth and support that surrounded Liadan. And this was never explained or reflected upon, just merely stated, and by Liadan to make it worse. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Excuse my vulgarity, but what a cold-hearted bitch! And then, without any discernible development or breakthrough moment, Liadan takes a U-turn in order to be the merciful saviour. She had to, otherwise the whole sweater would fall apart. As it is, it remains badly stitched together.<br /><br /><b>Marillier played with the notion of destiny but couldn't make up her mind</b>. Liadan could alter it, her loved one also, to some extent, but others were not so lucky and so the only viable option for them was to meekly follow the predestined course. Descendant of traitors must be traitorous, sorcerous blood must come out, and so on and so forth. <b>It is also a book about trust</b>. Again, Liadan betrayed the trust of her sister, but never that of her lover, she trusts in one thing, and blindly, but only when it suits her, others she spurns. She also demands trust from others, rarely being able to provide more rationale for it besides the very convenient Sight. Sometimes not at all and without any apparent reason<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[like denying her lover the knowledge that he has fathered a child <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br /><b>Marillier can write, I grant you that, but the book is too long and badly composed</b>. While the love affair is credible, <b>Niamh's story is far more interesting and with more drama to it than the mundane romance between Liadan and the Painted Man. And yet, Niamh does not get the credit, she shimmers on the margins of the main plot and basically serves as a springboard for Liadan</b>. Furthermore, the main tale interspersed with other tales and tellings. It is all grand if you are an ardent fan of Celtic folklore. Surely, these are interesting, but if I wanted to know those, I'd read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2000904.Celtic_Tales_and_Legends" title="Celtic Tales and Legends by Nicola Baxter" rel="nofollow noopener">Celtic Tales and Legends</a> or some other encyclopedic account of Irish mythology and fable. Woe is me, as the <b>Son of the Shadows gave me a sort of the Irish version of the Arabian Nights</b>.<br /><br />As you see, the whole sweater is made of bad yarn: it breaks in the plies, there are knots in many skeins with the orphaned and unknitted plies sitting like snags on the knit side of the fabric, and the loosely spun fibers result in pilling while the colour is bleeding and stains. I would not recommend it, as the Daughter of the Forest is a perfect standalone. <br /><br />* Terminology shamelessly stolen from the ever creative <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/16141901-zaara" rel="nofollow noopener">Zaara</a> <br /><br />Other Sevenwaters books: <br /><br />1. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1484917615?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Daughter of the Forest</a><br />3. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1491522467?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Child of the Prophecy</a> <br />4. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1600030169" rel="nofollow noopener">Heir to Sevenwaters</a><br />5. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1600030180" rel="nofollow noopener">Seer of Sevewaters</a> <br />6. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2350126263" rel="nofollow noopener">Flame of Sevenwaters</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="458450489330515506" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_462487689" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/462487689" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/462487689?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer462487689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1347626292612718079">It is, for some reason, extraordinarily difficult for me to explain my feelings concerning this novel. <i>Son of the Shadows</i> is, as all the reviews proclaim, a worthy follow-up to <i>Daughter of the Forest.</i> In fact, both novels are so vastly different that it is practically impossible to compare them and, without a doubt, <i>Son of the Shadows</i> is a beautifully written story, just as heart-breaking and emotionally impactful as its predecessor. Yet, my feelings of awe for this piece are mixed in with guilt</span>
  <span id="freeText1347626292612718079" style="display:none">It is, for some reason, extraordinarily difficult for me to explain my feelings concerning this novel. <i>Son of the Shadows</i> is, as all the reviews proclaim, a worthy follow-up to <i>Daughter of the Forest.</i> In fact, both novels are so vastly different that it is practically impossible to compare them and, without a doubt, <i>Son of the Shadows</i> is a beautifully written story, just as heart-breaking and emotionally impactful as its predecessor. Yet, my feelings of awe for this piece are mixed in with guilty disappointment. I say guilty merely because the majority of my friends have found this to be as remarkable a story as the first, and I definitely thought the first was a better novel, and disappointing because I went into this novel expecting it to be just as good, if not better, than its predecessor, and it wasn’t. Nevertheless, I will attempt to push aside my jumbled feelings and convey that, despite what I may have felt, this novel really was a masterpiece in and of itself. <br /><br /><i>Son of the Shadows</i> chronicles the story of Liadan, Sorcha’s daughter. It introduces us to Niamh, Sorcha’s eldest daughter, Sean, Sorcha’s only son and twin of Liadan, and Liadan herself who happens to be a seer. In Sevenwaters, Liadan’s life has been one of happiness and she, more than her siblings, has received the perfect mix of both her parents’ best qualities. Yet, disaster strikes Sevenwaters when, firstly, Sorcha falls ill and slowly begins her descent to death and later when Niamh is found to be having an affair with a man she is forbidden to be with. As such, Niamh is sent away for a profitable arranged marriage, accompanied by her sister, Liadan. On her way home, Liadan is kidnapped by the troop of the Painted Man, a notorious bandit who wants Liadan to cure his blacksmith. It is here that Liadan’s tale truly begins. <br /><br />What I loved about <i>Son of the Shadows</i> was the fact that, in many ways, it was the opposite of <i>Daughter of the Forest.</i> While <i>Daughter of the Forest</i> is a slow journey of trust, with every step taken one that is a little closer to happiness, <i>Son of the Shadows</i> is the unraveling of that trust and the plunge into darkness. Its themes, different from that of its predecessor, explore the true test of faith, of the multiple sides to every action, and of the importance of recognizing that one person’s happiness or correct path does not necessarily ensure happiness for another. It weaves a complex web of belief in others, one that is very fragile and easily broken, and the steady journey to see where each character winds up in the end and if they can survive and mend relationships despite hurdles is an interesting one to watch unfold. <br /><br />In addition to the themes itself, <i>Son of the Shadows</i> contains a very different kind of romance. In this, Liadan swiftly falls in love with one man, and he falls in love with her too, but the moment he finds out that she is from Sevenwaters, he instantly shuns her and refuses to have anything to do with her due to a past mistake of her father. As readers of <i>Daughter of the Forest,</i> it is impossible to understand why Bran, the Painted Man who falls in love with Liadan, could possibly hate Red and their love story, instead of being one in which the reader is waiting to see if the two characters truly love each other, is one where the reader is waiting to see if the two finally wind up together. I’ll admit that the nascence of this romance moved a little too quickly for me and I wasn’t able to form a solid bond with these two as a couple, but as the story wore on, they won me over and I can frankly admit that their love story is just as beautiful, moving, and powerful as that of Sorcha and Red. Furthermore, Bran is easily my favorite character in the tale, proving to be far more complex and tortured than I imagined and the build-up and eventual truth of his past definitely does not disappoint in the least. <br /><br />Nevertheless, despite its positives, <i>Son of the Shadows</i> certainly had a slew of negative aspects as well. Firstly, I have to state that Liadan experienced little to no character growth at all. When we first meet her, she is already an extremely well-developed character, but it is disappointing to see that her personality doesn’t experience much change despite the events she goes through. Instead, her siblings, Niamh and Sean, are much more flawed and humanely realistic than Liadan is, going through far more drastic stages of growth than she does. Yet, despite this, they don’t feature into enough of the storyline, making Liadan the sibling to love, and furthermore, they lack the strong bond between siblings that is so palpably felt between Sorcha and her brothers. In addition, some parts of this novel almost felt forced, most noticeably the drama. As a novel, it started and ended very strongly, but the middle, opposed to lagging, simply lacked something that left me rather detached from the tale overall. Where <i>Daughter of the Forest</i> made me feel like I was Sorcha herself and made me sob and weep and laugh and smile so much my face hurt, I was so consciously aware of reading a book while reading this. At times, Liadan's journey was just as powerful as her mother's, but during other times, it was simply a very good story. <br /><br />Overall, however, I can’t recommend this novel enough. Sure, it has its flaws, but the ultimate message it leaves you with, the character tales you won’t be able to forget, and the lore that never fails to captivate just cannot be missed. I’ve said it before and I’ll say it again – Juliet Marillier is a remarkable author. For any fan of her novels, this is a definite must-read. It lacks a little something that <i>Daughter of the Forest</i> had, but it is an excellent novel in its own right and it is one that I know I will return to and re-read in a few years, this time without that added expectation, and perhaps I will, after all, find it to be just as good as its predecessor at long last. <br /><br />You can read <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com/2013/01/review-son-of-shadows-sevenwaters-2-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">this review</a> and more on my blog, <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Ivy Book Bindings.</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="1347626292612718079" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Mikki Crisostomo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/373336-mikki-crisostomo"><img alt="Mikki Crisostomo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380164575p2/373336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6085560?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mikki Crisostomo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mikki Crisostomo" href="/user/show/373336-mikki-crisostomo">Mikki Crisostomo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/373336-mikki-crisostomo?shelf=books-i-would-die-for">books-i-would-die-for</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/373336-mikki-crisostomo?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/373336-mikki-crisostomo?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/373336-mikki-crisostomo?shelf=family">family</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6085560" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11211061268677988307">This is my favorite book of all time. My copy is dog-eared, and I'm looking around for another one. This was the book that set me off on my love for Juliet Marillier's books. The simple elegance of the prose was the perfect voice for Liadan, the main character. The love between Bran and Liadan spoke to me the first time I read it and has echoed deeper and deeper with every reading (of which there are many). In my opinion, this is better than the other two because the characters all have a way of</span>
  <span id="freeText11211061268677988307" style="display:none">This is my favorite book of all time. My copy is dog-eared, and I'm looking around for another one. This was the book that set me off on my love for Juliet Marillier's books. The simple elegance of the prose was the perfect voice for Liadan, the main character. The love between Bran and Liadan spoke to me the first time I read it and has echoed deeper and deeper with every reading (of which there are many). In my opinion, this is better than the other two because the characters all have a way of worming themselves into your heart.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11211061268677988307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1208803555" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1208803555" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1208803555?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Melina Marchetta</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Robin by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=book-boyfriend-material">book-boyfriend-material</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with">chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=quit-crying-robin">quit-crying-robin</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1208803555" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17782991153651099117"><b>Buddy read with the amazing <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10336538-jessica-rabid-reads' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jessica</a></b><br/><blockquote>
  <b><i>”I have believed, for a long time, that the Fair Folk guide our steps. That they work their great plans through us. But you are not in their scheme. Perhaps you hold some sort of key.”</i><br/><br/>╰⊰✿Overall Feelings On Son of Shadows✿⊱╮</b>
</blockquote><br/>Just like Daughter of the Forest this takes us on a magical and epic journey over years. Liadan like her mother is a healer and as with all the children of Sevenwaters has a deep capacity for love. Once she finds it she will hold onto it</span>
  <span id="freeText17782991153651099117" style="display:none"><b>Buddy read with the amazing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10336538-jessica-rabid-reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Jessica</a></b><br /><blockquote>
  <b><i>”I have believed, for a long time, that the Fair Folk guide our steps. That they work their great plans through us. But you are not in their scheme. Perhaps you hold some sort of key.”</i><br /><br />╰⊰✿Overall Feelings On Son of Shadows✿⊱╮</b>
</blockquote><br />Just like Daughter of the Forest this takes us on a magical and epic journey over years. Liadan like her mother is a healer and as with all the children of Sevenwaters has a deep capacity for love. Once she finds it she will hold onto it forever no matter the cost. They are not the heroines that we normally see in fantasy with great powers or skill with weapons and fighting. Yet each is so strong in their own way. <br /><br />This is an emotional journey, perhaps not quite as emotional as Daughter of the Forest but still <b>it took me through every emotion I have in my personal spectrum</b>. I get so caught up in the world that I felt like I took the journey as well and I couldn’t help racing through the story. There were two scene in particular that just gutted me. Again it is a darker fantasy than some and there are no neatly tied up bows at the end for all the characters involved. There are some happier endings than others and like life no one gets everything they want, some very hard choices had to be made.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>╰⊰✿The Story✿⊱╮</b>
</blockquote><br />Son of Shadows continues the story of Daughter of the Forest a generation later. Red and Sorcha have had three children and they are of an age when things really start to happen again. Whether that is because the Fae have set new plans in motion, or an ancient evil has a plan for revenge, or something even older than the Fae has plans of its own is unclear. <b> The only thing that is certain is a new challenge has been set and new dangers await the children of Sevenwaters</b>.<br /><br />Liadan is instantly likable, probably the most likable of all the three children Red and Sorcha had together. She is a reflection of both Sorcha and Red and I saw it in all of her choices and actions.<br /><blockquote>
  <i> “I can see we have taught you well, Liadan,” said my mother, regarding me closely. “You have my skill with healing and your father’s gift for love. He gathers all around him under his protective shade like a great forest tree. I see the same strength in you, Daughter.”</i>
</blockquote><br />All the children grew up sheltered in the love of Sevenwaters but when events are set in motion secrets from the past and some choices made separate the family in ways they never imagined before. The nice thing about Son of Shadows is that it starts out a little faster than Daughter of the Forest. The propelling events of the story happen almost immediately and carry Liadan into her destiny which was a little unexpected.<br /><br />Liadan is blessed and cursed as Finbar was with the gift of sight. It is while she is discovering her power in this that she is kidnapped by a band of mercenaries in hopes she can heal one of their men. When she first meets the Painted Man she believes him to be the heartless killer of all the tales. He plays the role well and only when Liadan is able to see into his mind and future does she see that maybe he could be more than just the man from the stories and his past is more tragic than anyone she has met before. Because of her gift Liadan might not know what the future holds exactly but she does know that they are intertwined<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“He and I—we share a bond. Not love, exactly. It goes beyond that. He is mine as surely as sun follows moon across the sky. Mine before ever I knew he existed. Mine until death and beyond. He is in terrible danger. From others and from himself. If I could do more to protect him, I would.</i>
</blockquote><br />This is more a tale of mending long time hurts and discovering a new path in life that might be different than what you always expected for yourself. Liadan must learn how to use her gifts with the help of Finbar if she is ever going to save the man who stole her heart and she discovers that it is a heavy task to be shown the possibilities of the future.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>╰⊰✿Why I Love the Sevenwaters World✿⊱╮</b>
</blockquote><br />One of the things that draws me into the Sevenwaters stories so much is the actual world. It has a mysticism to it. It is subtle and even believable in a sense where sorcerers and druids use nature to influence their surroundings. It is a place where a forest is a living breathing thing full of spirits and enchantments and the Fae are just a thin veil away. It is a place of prophecy and destiny and I do love a tale with a good but of destiny in it.<br /><br />I really like that these are tales of families and all the joy and complications that come from that. The people you love the most are the people that you are capable of hurting even when all you are doing is trying to help. The entanglements are so emotional and heartfelt that I fall into the story and don’t want to emerge from it even when it is over.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>╰⊰✿A Few Small Issues✿⊱╮</b>
</blockquote><br />These are books I have to be a little patient with. There are a lot of little building steps that do add to the story but sometimes make it seem like it is moving along slowly. In Daughter of the Forest this happened near the beginning and while Sorcha was alone before meeting Red. In Son of Shadow this happens in the middle.<br /><br />I spent a lot of time waiting and wanting Bran to come back into Liadan’s life. It felt like he was gone forever and I missed him. <b>I’m not saying this is necessarily a bad thing as it is probably what the author intended me to feel. The longing that Liadan felt for the man she knew she loved and I definitely felt that but I spent a lot of time waiting for him to come back</b> so I was a little distracted from what was happening while I was waiting. <br /><br />The other issue is that the villians of the story are sometimes a little over the top. I love a good villain but I like it the best when they can in a different light be seen as a possible hero if you are on the other side. Ciaran is a great example of this. He is likable and I understand his motivations but he is also someone that could be very dangerous in the future. <br /><br />Lastly the ending was slightly anticlimactic because of the nature of how Liadan saves Bran. It is more an internal struggle with his past and so not very action oriented. It is not entirely a bad thing either but I really would have enjoyed seeing Bran battle someone first hand.<br /><br />All of these are just small issues and why it wasn’t quite a 5 star read for me. <br /><br /><b>Note:</b>This can be read as a standalone novel. It is more enjoyable if you know who the older generation in and their story but it isn’t completely necessary.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17782991153651099117" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_167647699" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167647699" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167647699?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167647699" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10054163371033811055">I didn’t end up liking this one as much as <u>Daughter of the Forest</u>. I feel like with Juliet Marillier, it’s a clear case of “it’s not you, it’s me”. The writing is beautiful, and I love the Irish history and mythology, but these stories will just never be my favorites. <br/><br/>Sorcha’s daughter Liadan is the lead in this sequel, but she’s a bit of a carbon copy of her mother. She looks exactly like her, she’s an herbal healer, she has a brother with whom she shares a special mind link and bond, she falls</span>
  <span id="freeText10054163371033811055" style="display:none">I didn’t end up liking this one as much as <u>Daughter of the Forest</u>. I feel like with Juliet Marillier, it’s a clear case of “it’s not you, it’s me”. The writing is beautiful, and I love the Irish history and mythology, but these stories will just never be my favorites. <br /><br />Sorcha’s daughter Liadan is the lead in this sequel, but she’s a bit of a carbon copy of her mother. She looks exactly like her, she’s an herbal healer, she has a brother with whom she shares a special mind link and bond, she falls in love with the enemy of her family, she has the quiet strength of endurance and mental fortitude…. I really liked <u>Daughter of the Forest</u>, and there have definitely been repetitive series that I have loved anyway, but I got bored a few times in this one. Liadan must maneuver her way around her uncles, the faerie, the old ones, and her enemies as they all await the prophecy that will restore the islands to the family of Sevenwaters at last. <br /> <br />This is the second time that I have read a Juliet Marillier novel that made my expectations and hopes soar but didn’t deliver. In the first, I was disappointed by the lack of comeuppance for any of the black as night villians. In this one, I was so intrigued and excited by the prospect of a fighting heroine. Liadan tells the reader right from the beginning that she is trained in bow and staff, and can hold her own in a fight. Then, when challenged to show her skill, she performs a small feat of archery. I was so looking forward to the scene where she finally gets to use these skills for real, in a big showdown of some sort preferably. But, it never happens. In fact, she never uses her alleged fighting skills once in the whole book. I am not sure why it’s even mentioned that she has them! Liadan is a heroine in the same mold as Sorcha, and I guess I just prefer my heroines to be a bit more aggressive.<br /><br />Also, I admit that I was feeling pretty frustrated with the relationship between Liadan and Bran. They meet and spend <i>one week</i> together during which she discovers that he has a troubled past and he is insulting and dismissive. Then they share one night together and all of a sudden, it’s love. So, I was feeling a bit disgruntled with the whole affair, until I read this:<br /><br /><i>”He and I – we share a bond. Not love, exactly. It goes beyond that. He is mine as surely as sun follows moon across the sky.”</i><br /><br />Okay! So it’s not love! It’s some sort of mystical connection. I guess I can handle that. Now, to look forward to all of the scenes where they finally get to know one another and fall in love for reals. <br /><br />Nope. That never happened either.<br /><br />Liadan also really frustrated me a few times. Like when she judges her uncles so harshly for withholding key information from everyone, but then does the <i>exact same thing</i> to her brother Sean and her father…or when she inexplicably decides to take her infant child into immediate and terrible danger.<br /><br />It’s not all bad though – I did like this book as a whole. Niamh could have so easily been thrown away as a simple prop to show how virtuous and unselfish Liadan is by comparison. I love that Liadan and by extension, the author, don’t give up on her. She became one of my favorite characters and I would have liked to see more of her journey – she had a real progression. I also love that Juliet Marillier begins to explore the theme of genetic inheritance and destiny. Although, I am not so sure where she comes out on that – is she saying that people can escape the legacy of their evil parents or not? Her characters actually seem to prove that they can’t. I guess the jury’s still out on <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ciaran <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> though. Speaking of which, I have no knowledge of the plot of <u>Child of the Prophecy</u>, but how could Liadan fail to notice that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[there are actually two people that bear the sign of the crow, and two potential children that could fit the prophecy. She didn’t even notice the guy with an ACTUAL CROW!! Also, I’m sorry…but I don’t believe for one second that Juliet Marillier will have a male MC for the last book. She’s all about the quiet, enduring ladies. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I guess I only have one more thing to add: I hate the names for the heroes. For the rest of my life, I will picture a giant stick of cinnamon gum and a bowl of super colon blow.<br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />Florence + The Machine – <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2EIeUlvHAiM" rel="nofollow noopener">Cosmic Love</a> <br /><br />I listened to this album so obsessively last year that my two little girls can both sing along to almost all the words of Dog Days Are Over. This song has a bit of a new age-y feel that reminds me of these books. Also, the lyrics really couldn’t be more perfect!<br /><br /><i>I took the stars from our eyes, and then I made a map<br />I knew that somehow, I could find my way back<br />Then I heard your heart beating, you were in the darkness too<br />So I stayed in the darkness with you</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10054163371033811055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1211300151" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1211300151" />
    <a title="Choko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27962805-choko"><img alt="Choko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475642755p2/27962805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1211300151?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1211300151" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13242321554396783337"><b>*** 3.25 ***<br/><br/>A buddy read with my friends at FBR! Because we love Fantasy!!! </b><br/><br/>Another one of those books I should have been crazy about, but it some how missed the mark with me... And this time I know for sure it is me, because I just didn't connect with or liked the main character... Although at first glance Sorcha from the first book should have been very much like her daughter Liadan, the main POV here, I rooted for Sorcha and I had a deep connection with her, while Liadan was distant and judgm</span>
  <span id="freeText13242321554396783337" style="display:none"><b>*** 3.25 ***<br /><br />A buddy read with my friends at FBR! Because we love Fantasy!!! </b><br /><br />Another one of those books I should have been crazy about, but it some how missed the mark with me... And this time I know for sure it is me, because I just didn't connect with or liked the main character... Although at first glance Sorcha from the first book should have been very much like her daughter Liadan, the main POV here, I rooted for Sorcha and I had a deep connection with her, while Liadan was distant and judgmental, making it really hard to even like her, let alone develop any attachment to her... Liadan has a twin brother who is being raised to be the next Lord of Sevenwaters and with whom she has this deep mental connection and closeness. SHe also has an older sister, Niamh, who is not perfect, but not much different than any young woman in her teens battered by hormones, and the family, including Liadan, treat her and judge her very harshly, getting rid of her in a cold hearted way and washing their hands off of her, while for same types of indescretions and willfulness Liadan gets reproachful looks and reassurances that she could never disappoint them and they will love her no matter what... I expected better from Red and Sorcha as parents and from their offspring. However, I guess this is the whole point - none are perfect and all new generations have to solve some old wrongs and get new wrongs done to be dealt by the next generations... <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“Your actions are your own. Your choices are your own. Each of us carries a burden of guilt for decisions made or not made. You can let that rule your whole life or you can put it behind you and move on. Only a madman lets jealousy determine the course of his existence. Only a weak man blames others for his own errors.” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />The setting for this series is based on the British Isles and Celtic Myth, with some vague allusions to Brit History. The family who rules in Sevenwaters is descendant from a human and one of the Old Ones, thus it has a deep connection with the mystical lure in the land and all that grows there. They have been responsible for bringing the Druid religion back and at times communicate with the Fae, thus magic always plays a role in what happens with them. With the Brits and Christianity becoming more and more prevalent and taking over sacred Isles, the magic traditions and existence are threatened and Sorcha and her family have become of interest to all players involved, being used as a tool on one side or the other. Liadan is the child that was born outside of the predicted pattern and is much freer in making choices for her future. SHe takes full advantage of that when she meets a mysterious mercenary and his gang, and her view of the future changes dramatically. This leaves people feeling betrayed, alliances broken and new patterns are being created, for good or ill. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“Don't you long for something different to happen, something so exciting and new it carries you along with it like a great tide, something that lets your life blaze and burn so the whole world can see it? Something that touches you with joy or with terror, that lifts you out of your safe, little path and onto a great, wild road whose ending nobody knows? Don't you ever long for that?” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />Be careful what you wish for...!<br /><br />This book followed the general formula of the one which preceded it and that is not bad, I just missed all the emotional involvement I was amerced into with the first one. Liadan was only a pale imitation of Sorcha and only the cameo appearances of the uncles and the gang of mercenaries made up for that. I loved the big brutes with great hearts and I was enchanted by the lyrically magical presence of the uncle who has one arm and one Swan wing... The prose was beautiful as always, but the constant repetition of the belief that true love does not exist, but is an enchantment, a spell the woman casts on the man so he loves and wants to please her at all times, pisses me off!!! Once again! I am going to have to add a shelf for books which seem to make this an acceptable believe, and I just don't want to, since I want that to go away... Thank you for calling all women who have ever been loved witches, as in all times of human history!!! I am really going to have to accept that I am a witch and get over it, I guess:):):)<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“The world is simple, I think, in its essence. Life, death, love, hate. Desire, fulfillment. Magic.” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />I am planing on reading on, since the storytelling is really engaging and once I start the books, I can't put them down. So, if you love Fantasy with Celtic Mythology and Romance, this is a series you should check and see if it works for you! <br /><br />Now I wish you Happy Reading and may you always find what you Need in the pages of a Good Book!!! </span>
  <a data-text-id="13242321554396783337" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1692317748" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7608679771521147254">An outstanding book that continues the story of the children of Sevenwaters, and another for my favourites shelf.<br/><br/>The story of Sevenwaters continues with the children of Sorcha and Red. Whatever idyllic start Sevenwaters gives its children, they certainly are expected to shoulder more than their fair share of trial and difficulty as they grow up.<br/><br/>Liadan demonstrates the same fortitude her mother displayed in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13928.Daughter_of_the_Forest__Sevenwaters___1_' title='Daughter of the Forest (Sevenwaters, #1) by Juliet Marillier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Daughter of the Forest</a> as she makes her way through a path of treachery and hurt in order </span>
  <span id="freeText7608679771521147254" style="display:none">An outstanding book that continues the story of the children of Sevenwaters, and another for my favourites shelf.<br /><br />The story of Sevenwaters continues with the children of Sorcha and Red. Whatever idyllic start Sevenwaters gives its children, they certainly are expected to shoulder more than their fair share of trial and difficulty as they grow up.<br /><br />Liadan demonstrates the same fortitude her mother displayed in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13928.Daughter_of_the_Forest__Sevenwaters___1_" title="Daughter of the Forest (Sevenwaters, #1) by Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Daughter of the Forest</a> as she makes her way through a path of treachery and hurt in order to protect what she loves. The path she walks is only part of the story, however, and the road ahead remains filled with uncertainty and danger. <br /><br />This book fulfilled every expectation I had, delivering an amazing and richly imagined tale told with Marillier's trademark excellence and style.</span>

<div id="review_193230316" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/193230316" />
    <a title="Kay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5611008-kay"><img alt="Kay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314169555p2/5611008.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/193230316?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kay" href="/user/show/5611008-kay">Kay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">historical romance lovers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Kay by: </span>
      the first book
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5611008-kay?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5611008-kay?shelf=formidable-women">formidable-women</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5611008-kay?shelf=quite-the-romantic">quite-the-romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5611008-kay?shelf=faerie-poop">faerie-poop</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer193230316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13197798179609932669">I devoured this book. Once I started reading it, I couldn't stop, and I finished the book in about fifteen hours with breaks in between. It made me wonder why it took me so long to read this second installment to the Sevenwaters series, though the answer came to me pretty quickly as I was reading. To explain why this is, I have to start off with my experience with the first book. <br/><br/>The first book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13928.Daughter_of_the_Forest__Sevenwaters___1_' title='Daughter of the Forest (Sevenwaters, #1) by Juliet Marillier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Daughter of the Forest</a>, was an emotional journey. It was a tale about family, sacrifice, suffering, v</span>
  <span id="freeText13197798179609932669" style="display:none">I devoured this book. Once I started reading it, I couldn't stop, and I finished the book in about fifteen hours with breaks in between. It made me wonder why it took me so long to read this second installment to the Sevenwaters series, though the answer came to me pretty quickly as I was reading. To explain why this is, I have to start off with my experience with the first book. <br /><br />The first book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13928.Daughter_of_the_Forest__Sevenwaters___1_" title="Daughter of the Forest (Sevenwaters, #1) by Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Daughter of the Forest</a>, was an emotional journey. It was a tale about family, sacrifice, suffering, violence, and strength. It was about pushing the very limits of endurance, almost to the breaking point, until when all I wanted was to hold my hands up in defeat for Sorcha and ask wearily for the easy way out, even <i>knowing</i> that the alternative was to lose everything. But even for all that, the tale was beautiful, magical, and romantic. The book affected me deeply and twisted my emotions so that I needed some breathing time to unwind before diving headfirst into another Sevenwaters book.<br /><br />Only recently did I buck up and decide that it was time to pick up the second installment. I was expecting more epic feats of human endurance, something that would twist and overturn my heart. I was, perhaps misguidedly, expecting another <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13928.Daughter_of_the_Forest__Sevenwaters___1_" title="Daughter of the Forest (Sevenwaters, #1) by Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Daughter of the Forest</a>. <br /><br />But it was not to be. <br /><br />Don’t get me wrong. I really enjoyed Son of the Shadows. It was very well written, and the plot was interesting. It was a strong follow-up to the first, and I was more than pleasantly surprised at the paths it took. <br /><br />However, if the first book is the ocean during a torrential storm, this book is more like a calm lake during an autumn drizzle. Liadan, the main character, is the model protagonist. Perfect, but not to the point of being annoying. She is the heart of Sevenwaters, repeated several times verbatim in the book. She is strong, loyal, fair-minded, and wise beyond her years. She’s a character that doesn’t require much development because she’s already very developed from the beginning. Bran, Liadan's foil, is similar. He is a haunted man, but aside from his past, you can tell he’s an otherwise perfect male lead. He’s someone who clearly requires the healing skills of Liadan to mend that gaping gap of “imperfect” before he can become a worthy companion to Liadan. It was fun reading about the two because, despite their difficulties, I already <i>knew</i> in the back of my mind, that they would come through somehow. I suspect this is why I got through this book so quickly.<br /><br />Also, it was easier for me to orient myself emotionally in this novel. One of the main themes was authority. Women were much more susceptible to the whims of men, both in politics and the family unit. So were young children victim to the whims of adults. While this is a fair issue to explore, it was a constricting setup and somewhat at odds with the other theme of “deciding one’s own destiny.” Liadan’s birth, after all, was not foreseen, and thus she is an anomaly, someone who can change things, whatever that means. But the constant mention and examples of women being subject to the desires of men became obvious very fast. In short, authority = bad (most of the time); finding one's own path = good.<br /><br />The romance was also pretty direct. The attraction between Liadan and Bran is prevalent as soon as they meet gazes. They were much more physical than Sorcha and Red, which was a refreshing change, but they also faced less hardships. The depth of emotion between the two, while strong, did not reach the shadowy depths of Sorcha’s and Red’s. I still enjoyed reading about Liadan and Bran, though their relationship was not as memorable as their predecessors’. <br /><br />In sum, this book lacked the subtlety and depth of the first, but considering all other factors, it was still a very good story. The writing is strong, the characters are strong (albeit a little too perfect or a little too flawed), and the story itself is strong. I found that this book read more like a historical romance novel but with more spirit, less bodice ripping, and much more of a gripping storyline. Some of the reveals towards the end of the book, especially Niamh’s and Ciaran’s, are definitely WTF-worthy. <br /><br />Overall, a <b> SOLID 4 STARS</b>. <br /><br />Definitely buying the third book asap. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13197798179609932669" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
