<div id="review_38887446" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38887446" />
    <a title="Meredith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/994742-meredith"><img alt="Meredith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573166402p2/994742.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/38887446?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith" href="/user/show/994742-meredith">Meredith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38887446" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2937251172692080218">Meh. I wish she hadn’t made it a series. So why did I give it 3 stars? It was well written—I like Miss Marillier’s prose. <br/><br/>Now I will proceed to tell you why I gave it three stars instead of five.<br/><br/>Son of the Shadows didn’t flow well, and the characters were rather bland. They read like reheated character ideas she probably had for the last book, but threw out and decided to use for the sequel. That may be why this book felt a loooot like the last one: forbidden love, healer protagonist, protagonis</span>
  <span id="freeText2937251172692080218" style="display:none">Meh. I wish she hadn’t made it a series. So why did I give it 3 stars? It was well written—I like Miss Marillier’s prose. <br /><br />Now I will proceed to tell you why I gave it three stars instead of five.<br /><br />Son of the Shadows didn’t flow well, and the characters were rather bland. They read like reheated character ideas she probably had for the last book, but threw out and decided to use for the sequel. That may be why this book felt a loooot like the last one: forbidden love, healer protagonist, protagonist living away from home, protagonist doctors sick man, protagonist is a young female, etc.<br /><br />Also, the Ciaran/Niamh love story was more interesting than the Liadan/Bran story. Bran wasn’t even likeable. I mean, maybe if your type is the ultra-sensitive-but-hides-it-all-under-a-grumpy-and-gloomy-exterior kind of guy…but he also happens to be your family’s sworn enemy kind of guy…who also happens to be the kind of guy who just kidnapped you…who also happens to be the guy you’ve only known for less than a week! Really?!?<br /><br />P.S. What kind of name is ‘Bran’ for a leading hunk? <br />P.P.S. Rated R for sexual content. Not really a YA book.<br /><br />But it was well written. Despite all of that. :)</span>

<div id="review_95769853" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95769853" />
    <a title="Terry (Ter05 TwiMoms/ MundieMoms)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3043482-terry-ter05-twimoms-mundiemoms"><img alt="Terry (Ter05 TwiMoms/ MundieMoms)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364303580p2/3043482.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95769853?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Terry (Ter05 TwiMoms/ MundieMoms)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Terry (Ter05 TwiMoms/ MundieMoms)" href="/user/show/3043482-terry-ter05-twimoms-mundiemoms">Terry (Ter05 TwiMoms/ MundieMoms)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone- but read Daughter of the Forest first</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3043482-terry-ter05-twimoms-mundiemoms?shelf=could-not-put-it-down-books">could-not-put-it-down-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3043482-terry-ter05-twimoms-mundiemoms?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3043482-terry-ter05-twimoms-mundiemoms?shelf=ireland">ireland</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3043482-terry-ter05-twimoms-mundiemoms?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3043482-terry-ter05-twimoms-mundiemoms?shelf=read-more-than-once">read-more-than-once</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3043482-terry-ter05-twimoms-mundiemoms?shelf=favorite-series">favorite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3043482-terry-ter05-twimoms-mundiemoms?shelf=love-the-audio">love-the-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3043482-terry-ter05-twimoms-mundiemoms?shelf=epic-series">epic-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3043482-terry-ter05-twimoms-mundiemoms?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3043482-terry-ter05-twimoms-mundiemoms?shelf=magic">magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95769853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14584016348555813630">[UPDATE: 6/2018 Re-read for probably the tenth time. I can pick this book up any time and not be able to put it down. First read in 2012 I changed one tag from romance to love story. Maybe the same but romance seems trite compared to this kind of love. I mentioned below, the that Bran and Liadan are apart for probably 3/4 of the book. Maybe that is what makes this book so powerful. I will continue to read it over and over again through the years.]<br/><br/>This is what I consider a ten star book. I am rew</span>
  <span id="freeText14584016348555813630" style="display:none">[UPDATE: 6/2018 Re-read for probably the tenth time. I can pick this book up any time and not be able to put it down. First read in 2012 I changed one tag from romance to love story. Maybe the same but romance seems trite compared to this kind of love. I mentioned below, the that Bran and Liadan are apart for probably 3/4 of the book. Maybe that is what makes this book so powerful. I will continue to read it over and over again through the years.]<br /><br />This is what I consider a ten star book. I am rewriting my review after reading this for the third time and after having read the entire series. [November 2014 - just listened to the audio - awesome as the read!] There are a lot of wonderful authors out there, but not nearly as many master story-tellers. Juliet Marillier is exactly that. This is the second in the Sevenwaters series and set in 4th century Ireland. Reading this for the second time, I was questioning what made it such a beautiful read. It is an unforgettable romance and yet Bran and Liadan are apart for much of the book. Or are they? When two people are bound the way this outlaw and the innocent daughter of Sevenwaters are, are they ever truly apart? Liadan is an amazing strong female character which is so common in this author's books. But with the gift of "sight", an ability to communicate through the mind with her twin brother, Sean, and at times with Bran, she often considers her gifts to be a curse because of the confusion they cause. Throughout the book she carries secrets that if exposed could cause the death of loved ones and maybe the destruction of her entire world. Should her loyalty be to family, to the faery Queen and her consort who clearly instruct her as to what she should do, to the "old ones" who were there since the beginning of time and who she is descended from? Or should her loyalty be to the man she loves, the Painted Man, and reviled outlaw. And how can what Liadan desires fit in? She is told that she can't have the two most important things in her life, but she is determined not to give up either one. This is the story of Liadan's choices, her bravery, and her love. <br /><br />This book is meant to be read following Daughter of the Forest which is the story of Red and Sorcha, Liadan's parents. They and the rest of her family that we knew in Daughter of the Forest are with her as well as new characters. Her uncle, Finbar, is a part of this story as he lives between the mortal world and the otherworld with his swan wing as the result of a curse in the previous book. Finbar is the rock she clings to when all seems so confused and twisted. Having read the following books, Finbar remains a central figure and spiritual part of the Sevenwaters story. Another new character that remains in the next books is the young Druid, Ciaran. His story is tragic and closely connected to the previous book - and to the books to come. The first time I read this book I thought the son of the shadows was Liadan's Bran. But two re-reads later I realize that it is Ciaran, and that makes more sense even though he is not the main character of this book. I love the way each book in this series is the story of another couple in the Sevenwaters saga and yet includes ongoing stories of those we learn to love in each book. <br /><br />[Comment from my second reading in 2011] - Master story teller. I had read this book before and yet sat up until 1:30 this morning reading to the end because I could not put it down. It is my favorite of the series but they are all wonderful.<br /><br />[Comment from my third reading in 2012] - I had not re-read Daughter of the Forest until this week, and it was so compelling that I had to pick up this book and re-read it for the third time. I had to laugh at my comment above - I read it this time in less than 24 hours and hardly put it down. I marked a few favorite quotes that perhaps give a sample of this author's writing.<br /><br />Liadan: "So I rode back to Sevenwaters on the Painted Man's horse, with his coat to keep me warm, with a necklace of wolf claws in my pocket and blood on my hands. So much for being able to change things. So much for the Fair Folk and ancient voices and visions of death. What was I but one more powerless woman in a world of unthinking men? Nothing had changed. Nothing at all, save deep inside,where nobody could see."<br /><br />Liadan to Sorcha: "I did not journey beyond he margins, Mother, though I did see the Fair Folk, and they spoke to me. This child's father is a mortal man, and I will not give his name."<br /><br />Sorcha's brother, Finbar to Liadan: "I am the beat of a swan's wing on the breath of the wind. I am the secret at the heart of the standing stone. I am the island in the wild sea. I am the fire in the head of the seer. I am neither of that world nor of this. And yet, I am a man. I have blood on my hands. I have loved and lost. I feel your pain, and and know your strength."<br /><br /><br />Finbar again, " Oh yes. And he saw you, make no doubt of it. But that is nothing new to him. Your image is before his eyes through every battle, through every flight, through every subtle knife stroke, through every long dark night. You bound him to you with your courage and with your tales. You hold him to you now. You captured a wild creature when you had no place you could keep him. He cannot escape you, however hard he might wish it to be otherwise."</span>
  <a data-text-id="14584016348555813630" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1015103460" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1015103460" />
    <a title="Cayla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1926715-cayla"><img alt="Cayla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339546283p2/1926715.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1015103460?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cayla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cayla" href="/user/show/1926715-cayla">Cayla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1015103460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2198448317122577457">*Spoilers*<br/><br/>I found this book incredibly disappointing, especially in comparison to the quality of Daughter of the Forest. I read another review where the reader said she hated this book because the author made the main character, Liadan, too perfect. I generally agree with this comment in that I believe the author's intent was to make Liadan perfect, but what was even more annoying about this book was that all the characters complimented Liadan constantly, often without merit. The compliments nev</span>
  <span id="freeText2198448317122577457" style="display:none">*Spoilers*<br /><br />I found this book incredibly disappointing, especially in comparison to the quality of Daughter of the Forest. I read another review where the reader said she hated this book because the author made the main character, Liadan, too perfect. I generally agree with this comment in that I believe the author's intent was to make Liadan perfect, but what was even more annoying about this book was that all the characters complimented Liadan constantly, often without merit. The compliments never stopped! Finbar asked Liadan to have the dogs put away and mentioned he didn't want to tell anyone except her his fear - I think in an attempt to show that Liadan was the only understanding person in the whole family. So she went and told Liam Finbar's fear and asked him to put away the dogs (wasn't she supposed to not tell Finbar's fear?), and Liam tells Liadan how great she is. Did she really do something THAT wonderful. This was constant throughout the book. No matter what she did, the author took a moment to have some character tell Liadan how great she was. I felt like she was the epitome of the favorite child who could do no wrong. <br /><br />I also thought the author gave Liadan too many powers. In Sorcha's generation, the seven siblings seemed to split the powers. Finbar could see into the future and had strong mental powers, Conor was the druid, Liam was the strong leader, Sorcha was the healer (with some mental powers), etc. Also, the powers Sorcha did have were limited by the facts that her brothers were swans and she could not speak. Now comes the next generation. Liadan seems to get all the powers with absolutely no limits due to circumstances. She had strong mental abilities, could see the future, was a healer, and seemed to have a way of making everyone love her. It just made everything she did seem ridiculous. <br /><br />I found it disappointing that the author didn't really try to develop any other characters. Sorcha and Red had three children: Niamh, Sean, and Liadan. The author tried to give Liadan every good quality and made Niamh and Sean worthless characters. Niamh was just the depthless flirt who didn't even realize her mother was dying. I think the author tried to throw some good qualities to Sean, but he slapped Niamh and when Liadan asked Niamh to sit by her to get her away from her husband, Sean tells Liadan not to intervene. The author almost used these characters to make Liadan seem even better and more perfect, but it just made me more annoyed at Liadan being such the favorite child of the author.<br /><br />Coming back to the fact that Liadan had too many powers, it also made some parts of the story unbelievable. I had assumed that Liadan could only speak mentally with Sean within a certain distance. I assumed this was why she did not call out to Sean when she was captured. When the painted man sent her away, however, we find out she could just call out to Sean and show him where she was. Why didn't she do that right away? She tells us she didn't do that to protect the outlaws, but when she was first captured, she had no idea they would be nice to her. Some of her men were killed protecting her, she knew that her family would be looking for her, wouldn't she, at the very least, tell Sean she was okay? Seems a little selfish not to send out that message (a flaw of this "perfect" character). Then when she thinks she'll never get to go home, why wouldn't she call out then? It just made no sense. <br /><br />Further, I hated Liadan's romance with the painted man and found it very unbelievable. Especially in the time Liadan lived in, going off at 16 and getting pregnant by an outlaw was not a great thing. If she was such a perfect character, I just don't think this would have happened, especially after she had seen Niamh get married off for doing what appeared to be the same thing. If the painted man was such a great guy, he wouldn't have slept with an innocent 16-year-old, especially since it was against his "code." The painted man then finds out who Liadan is and is very rude to her and sends her off. I think this would have hurt Liadan slightly more. It seemed to barely phase her at all. Unrealistic. Then she goes home and tells her parents she's pregnant, and their response is to tell her they're excited about the baby and trust her. I know the point of the book was for everyone to compliment Liadan from start to finish, but that seemed a bit overboard. <br /><br />Finally, I found it confusing whether Liadan and the painted man were meant to have a baby together. Liadan sensed something bad would happen when they arrived at the shelter in the woods. The night she slept with the painted man, the ancient voices encouraged her to stay by him, which she was later told she shouldn't have listened to. However, it then seems like the baby was supposed to be created. This was never clear.<br /><br />I do feel bad overly criticizing this book, but I think what made me really mad was that it took away from the magic of the first book. The first book was so amazing and I wish I had just left the story there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2198448317122577457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+s320r25zeVqxAxM2tBO7LsF0toaTIEwxQ7/eEsld5qgm03TW9umdxdMiKt5nUqDq064dLHsYUPWRAeKLTDj1w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8191336650250635879">Juliet Marillier was born in Dunedin, New Zealand and grew up surrounded by Celtic music and stories. Her own Celtic-Gaelic roots inspired her to write her first series, the Sevenwaters Trilogy. Juliet was educated at the University of Otago, where she majored in music and languages, graduating BA and Bachelor of Music (Hons). Her lifelong interest in history, folklore and mythology has had a majo</span>
  <span id="freeText8191336650250635879" style="display:none">Juliet Marillier was born in Dunedin, New Zealand and grew up surrounded by Celtic music and stories. Her own Celtic-Gaelic roots inspired her to write her first series, the Sevenwaters Trilogy. Juliet was educated at the University of Otago, where she majored in music and languages, graduating BA and Bachelor of Music (Hons). Her lifelong interest in history, folklore and mythology has had a major influence on her writing.<br /><br />Juliet is the author of twenty-one historical fantasy novels for adults and young adults, as well as a book of short fiction. Juliet's novels and short stories have won many awards. <br /><br />Juliet lives in a 110 year old cottage in a riverside suburb of Perth, Western Australia. When not writing, she tends to her small pack of rescue dogs. She also has four adult children and eight grandchildren. Juliet is a member of the druid order OBOD (the Order of Bards, Ovates and Druids.)<br /></span>
